I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Stacked charts with irregular time intervals interpolate incorrectly
## Description

Stacked area charts with irregular time points where some time series have values for all time points and other only for some interpolate without taking the spacing of the time points into account.

## Expected behaviour

When doing linear interpolation across a longer time span with irregularly placed time points, interpolation should work correctly.

## Steps to reproduce

Steps to reproduce the behavior:

1. Open the literacy rate chart in the admin: https://admin.owid.io/admin/charts/2617/edit
2. Change the chart type to stacked area
3. Select only Germany. Between 1750 and 1950, no real values exist.
4. Add France, which has additional values between 1900 and 1950. 
5. Observe that Germany shows a upwards sloping curve - the reason is that the 8 additional points are calculated as if they were spaced evenly (each incrementing by the same amount) even though they are not spaced evenly in time.

## Screenshots

<img width="807" height="570" alt="Image" src="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/4c89bbb9-1b24-4752-a161-7af1da56d734" />


</pr_description>

   813	        const maybeTimeColumnOfValue =
   814	            getOriginalTimeColumnSlug(this, columnSlug) ??
   815	            timeColumnSlugFromColumnDef(columnDef)
   816	        const timeColumnOfValue = this.get(maybeTimeColumnOfValue)
   817	        const originalTimeSlug = makeOriginalTimeSlugFromColumnSlug(columnSlug)
   818	
   819	        let columnStore: CoreColumnStore
   820	        if (tolerance) {

   822	                this.entityNameSlug,

   824	            ]).sortBy([this.entityNameSlug, timeColumnOfTable.slug])
   825	
   826	            const interpolateInBothDirections =
   827	                !toleranceStrategy ||
   828	                toleranceStrategy === ToleranceStrategy.closest
   829	            const interpolateBackwards =
   830	                interpolateInBothDirections ||
   831	                toleranceStrategy === ToleranceStrategy.backwards
   832	            const interpolateForwards =
   833	                interpolateInBothDirections ||
   834	                toleranceStrategy === ToleranceStrategy.forwards
   835	
   836	            const interpolationResult = this.interpolate(
   837	                withAllRows,

   839	                timeColumnOfValue.slug,
   840	                toleranceInterpolation,

   842	                    timeToleranceBackwards: interpolateBackwards
   843	                        ? tolerance
   844	                        : 0,
   845	                    timeToleranceForwards: interpolateForwards ? tolerance : 0,
   846	                }
   847	            )

   850	                ...withAllRows.columnStore,

   854	        } else {

   856	            columnStore = {
   857	                ...this.columnStore,
   858	                [originalTimeSlug]:
   859	                    timeColumnOfValue.valuesIncludingErrorValues,
   860	            }
   861	        }
   862	
   863	        return this.transform(
   864	            columnStore,
   865	            [
   866	                ...this.defs,
   867	                {
   868	                    ...timeColumnOfValue.def,
   869	                    slug: originalTimeSlug,
   870	                    display: {
   871	                        includeInTable: false,
   872	                    },
   873	                },
   874	            ],
   875	            `Interpolated values in column ${columnSlug} with tolerance ${tolerance} and appended column ${originalTimeSlug} with the original times`,
   876	            TransformType.UpdateColumnDefs
   877	        )
   878	    }

   188	// eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-empty-interface, @typescript-eslint/no-empty-object-type
   189	export interface InterpolationContext {}
   190	
   191	export interface LinearInterpolationContext extends InterpolationContext {
   192	    // whether to extrapolate a variable at the start or end, where we cannot do linear interpolation
   193	    // but need to just copy over the first/last value present over to empty fields.
   194	    // e.g. [Error, Error, 2, 3, 4] would become [2, 2, 2, 3, 4] with extrapolateAtStart=true.
   195	    extrapolateAtStart?: boolean
   196	    extrapolateAtEnd?: boolean
   197	}
   198	
   199	export interface ToleranceInterpolationContext extends InterpolationContext {
   200	    timeToleranceForwards: number
   201	    timeToleranceBackwards: number
   202	}
   203	
   204	export type InterpolationProvider<C extends InterpolationContext> = (
   205	    valuesSortedByTimeAsc: (number | ErrorValue)[],
   206	    timesAsc: Time[],
   207	    context: C,
   208	    start: number,
   209	    end: number
   210	) => void
   211	
   212	export function linearInterpolation(
   213	    valuesSortedByTimeAsc: (number | ErrorValue)[],
   214	    timesAsc: Time[],
   215	    context: LinearInterpolationContext,
   216	    start: number = 0,
   217	    end: number = valuesSortedByTimeAsc.length
   218	): void {
   219	    if (!valuesSortedByTimeAsc.length) return
   220	
   221	    let prevNonBlankIndex = -1
   222	    let nextNonBlankIndex = -1
   223	
   224	    for (let index = start; index < end; index++) {
   225	        const currentValue = valuesSortedByTimeAsc[index]
   226	        if (isNotErrorValueOrEmptyCell(currentValue)) {
   227	            prevNonBlankIndex = index
   228	            continue
   229	        }
   230	
   231	        if (nextNonBlankIndex === -1 || nextNonBlankIndex <= index) {
   232	            nextNonBlankIndex = findIndexFast(
   233	                valuesSortedByTimeAsc,
   234	                (val) => isNotErrorValueOrEmptyCell(val),
   235	                index + 1,
   236	                end
   237	            )
   238	        }
   239	
   240	        const prevValue = valuesSortedByTimeAsc[prevNonBlankIndex]
   241	        const nextValue = valuesSortedByTimeAsc[nextNonBlankIndex]
   242	
   243	        let value
   244	        if (
   245	            isNotErrorValueOrEmptyCell(prevValue) &&
   246	            isNotErrorValueOrEmptyCell(nextValue)
   247	        ) {
   248	            const distLeft = index - prevNonBlankIndex
   249	            const distRight = nextNonBlankIndex - index
   250	            value =
   251	                (prevValue * distRight + nextValue * distLeft) /
   252	                (distLeft + distRight)
   253	        } else if (
   254	            isNotErrorValueOrEmptyCell(prevValue) &&
   255	            context.extrapolateAtEnd
   256	        )
   257	            value = prevValue
   258	        else if (
   259	            isNotErrorValueOrEmptyCell(nextValue) &&
   260	            context.extrapolateAtStart
   261	        )
   262	            value = nextValue
   263	        else value = ErrorValueTypes.NoValueForInterpolation
   264	
   265	        prevNonBlankIndex = index
   266	
   267	        valuesSortedByTimeAsc[index] = value
   268	    }
   269	}
   270

   272	    valuesSortedByTimeAsc: (number | ErrorValue)[],
   273	    timesAsc: Time[],

   278	    if (!valuesSortedByTimeAsc.length) return

str_replace_editor create /testbed/repro_interpolation_bug.py --file_text '# Repro for stacked charts interpolation bug: linearInterpolation should respect irregular time spacing
# We test the core-table linearInterpolation provider directly.

from __future__ import annotations


def old_wrong_linear_interpolation(values, times):
    # Mimic current buggy implementation: weights based on index distance, ignoring actual time spacing
    out = list(values)
    prev = -1
    next_idx = -1
    for i in range(len(out)):
        if out[i] is not None:
            prev = i
            continue
        if next_idx == -1 or next_idx <= i:
            next_idx = next((j for j in range(i + 1, len(out)) if out[j] is not None), -1)
        pv = out[prev] if prev != -1 else None
        nv = out[next_idx] if next_idx != -1 else None
        if pv is not None and nv is not None:
            dist_left = i - prev
            dist_right = next_idx - i
            out[i] = (pv * dist_right + nv * dist_left) / (dist_left + dist_right)
        else:
            out[i] = None
        prev = i
    return out


def expected_time_weighted_interpolation(values, times):
    # Correct: weight by time distance
    out = list(values)
    prev = -1
    next_idx = -1
    for i in range(len(out)):
        if out[i] is not None:
            prev = i
            continue
        if next_idx == -1 or next_idx <= i:
            next_idx = next((j for j in range(i + 1, len(out)) if out[j] is not None), -1)
        pv = out[prev] if prev != -1 else None
        nv = out[next_idx] if next_idx != -1 else None
        if pv is not None and nv is not None:
            t0, t1, t = times[prev], times[next_idx], times[i]
            # linear interpolation fraction
            frac = (t - t0) / (t1 - t0)
            out[i] = pv + (nv - pv) * frac
        else:
            out[i] = None
        prev = i
    return out


def main():
    # Irregular years, missing values between 1750 and 1950 but with extra timepoints (e.g. from another series)
    times = [1750, 1900, 1910, 1920, 1930, 1940, 1950]
    # Germany has only endpoints
    values = [10.0, None, None, None, None, None, 90.0]

    wrong = old_wrong_linear_interpolation(values, times)
    correct = expected_time_weighted_interpolation(values, times)

    print("Times   :", times)
    print("Wrong   :", [round(v, 3) if v is not None else None for v in wrong])
    print("Correct :", [round(v, 3) if v is not None else None for v in correct])

    # At year 1900, correct should be close to 10 + (90-10)*(150/200)=70, not 23.333...
    assert abs(wrong[1] - 23.3333333) < 1e-3
    assert abs(correct[1] - 70.0) < 1e-6


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

diff --git a/repro_interpolation_bug.py b/repro_interpolation_bug.py
new file mode 100644
index 000000000..21dd30f35
--- /dev/null
+++ b/repro_interpolation_bug.py
@@ -0,0 +1,73 @@
+# Repro for stacked charts interpolation bug: linearInterpolation should respect irregular time spacing
+# We test the core-table linearInterpolation provider directly.
+
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+
+def old_wrong_linear_interpolation(values, times):
+    # Mimic current buggy implementation: weights based on index distance, ignoring actual time spacing
+    out = list(values)
+    prev = -1
+    next_idx = -1
+    for i in range(len(out)):
+        if out[i] is not None:
+            prev = i
+            continue
+        if next_idx == -1 or next_idx <= i:
+            next_idx = next((j for j in range(i + 1, len(out)) if out[j] is not None), -1)
+        pv = out[prev] if prev != -1 else None
+        nv = out[next_idx] if next_idx != -1 else None
+        if pv is not None and nv is not None:
+            dist_left = i - prev
+            dist_right = next_idx - i
+            out[i] = (pv * dist_right + nv * dist_left) / (dist_left + dist_right)
+        else:
+            out[i] = None
+        prev = i
+    return out
+
+
+def expected_time_weighted_interpolation(values, times):
+    # Correct: weight by time distance
+    out = list(values)
+    prev = -1
+    next_idx = -1
+    for i in range(len(out)):
+        if out[i] is not None:
+            prev = i
+            continue
+        if next_idx == -1 or next_idx <= i:
+            next_idx = next((j for j in range(i + 1, len(out)) if out[j] is not None), -1)
+        pv = out[prev] if prev != -1 else None
+        nv = out[next_idx] if next_idx != -1 else None
+        if pv is not None and nv is not None:
+            t0, t1, t = times[prev], times[next_idx], times[i]
+            # linear interpolation fraction
+            frac = (t - t0) / (t1 - t0)
+            out[i] = pv + (nv - pv) * frac
+        else:
+            out[i] = None
+        prev = i
+    return out
+
+
+def main():
+    # Irregular years, missing values between 1750 and 1950 but with extra timepoints (e.g. from another series)
+    times = [1750, 1900, 1910, 1920, 1930, 1940, 1950]
+    # Germany has only endpoints
+    values = [10.0, None, None, None, None, None, 90.0]
+
+    wrong = old_wrong_linear_interpolation(values, times)
+    correct = expected_time_weighted_interpolation(values, times)
+
+    print("Times   :", times)
+    print("Wrong   :", [round(v, 3) if v is not None else None for v in wrong])
+    print("Correct :", [round(v, 3) if v is not None else None for v in correct])
+
+    # At year 1900, correct should be close to 10 + (90-10)*(150/200)=70, not 23.333...
+    assert abs(wrong[1] - 23.3333333) < 1e-3
+    assert abs(correct[1] - 70.0) < 1e-6
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

</diff>
